        "Now, putting aside for a moment the calculation method where weights are multiplied and summed to give values between 0 and 1 for the input and output parts,\n\nlet's return to the LSTM calculation process. First, if you look at the high-level input-output form, the original LSTMâ€”or when we refer to the original version of any modelâ€” is also called the vanilla model, meaning the most basic form. This is because vanilla ice cream is the most basic flavor of ice cream. Similarly, the LSTM model, like the vanilla RNN model, basically takes as input a concatenated vector consisting of the current time step input vector xâ‚œ and the previous time step hidden state vector hâ‚œâ‚‹â‚. Then, through a linear transformation, it creates output vectors. For example, when the dimensions of the input vector xâ‚œ and the hidden state vector hâ‚œâ‚‹â‚ are represented with absolute value symbols, the linear transformation via matrix multiplication generates four sets of vectors, each having the same dimension as the hidden state vector.\n\nFor these four vectors, the first three vectors each pass through a sigmoid operation, transforming their values to range between 0 and 1 for each timestep. The last, fourth vector passes through a tanh function, resulting in values between -1 and 1. These four vectors obtained this way are referred to as the input gate i, forget gate f, output gate o, and function output g, respectively.\n\nAfter calculating these four vectors, the previous time step's cell state vector câ‚œâ‚‹â‚ is updated to the current cell state vector câ‚œ using this formula. Here, the operation represented by the dot inside the circle denotes element-wise multiplication.\n\nThe updated câ‚œ is then passed through the tanh function at each timestep, generating values between -1 and 1. Finally, by element-wise multiplying this result with the output gate o at each timestep, the current timestep's hidden state vector hâ‚œ is computed."
      ]

        "ğ‘Š: Weight matrix\nâ„: Hidden state\nğ‘: Cell state\nğ‘¥: Input"
      ]
    }
  ]

      "content after edit": [
        "Now, putting aside for a moment the calculation method where weights are multiplied and summed to give values between 0 and 1 for the input and output parts,\n\nlet's return to the LSTM calculation process. First, if you look at the high-level input-output form, the original LSTMâ€”or when we refer to the original version of any modelâ€” is also called the vanilla model, meaning the most basic form. This is because vanilla ice cream is the most basic flavor of ice cream. Similarly, the LSTM model, like the vanilla RNN model, basically takes as input a concatenated vector consisting of the current time step input vector xâ‚œ and the previous time step hidden state vector hâ‚œâ‚‹â‚. Then, through a linear transformation, it creates output vectors. For example, when the dimensions of the input vector xâ‚œ and the hidden state vector hâ‚œâ‚‹â‚ are represented with absolute value symbols, the linear transformation via matrix multiplication generates four sets of vectors, each having the same dimension as the hidden state vector.\n\nFor these four vectors, the first three vectors each pass through a sigmoid operation, transforming their values to range between 0 and 1 for each timestep. The last, fourth vector passes through a tanh function, resulting in values between -1 and 1. These four vectors obtained this way are referred to as the input gate i, forget gate f, output gate o, and function output g, respectively.\n\nAfter calculating these four vectors, the previous time step's cell state vector câ‚œâ‚‹â‚ is updated to the current cell state vector câ‚œ using this formula. Here, the operation represented by the dot inside the circle denotes element-wise multiplication.\n\nThe updated câ‚œ is then passed through the tanh function at each timestep, generating values between -1 and 1. Finally, by element-wise multiplying this result with the output gate o at each timestep, the current timestep's hidden state vector hâ‚œ is computed."
      ]
